#  [](/thread/226349-odds-are-with-a-4hr-kiss)Odds are with a 4hr KISS 

  * 

  * [#1](/thread/226349-odds-are-with-a-4hr-kiss "Post Permalink")

  * First Post: Edited Oct 21, 2012 5:44am  Mar 17, 2010 2:01am | Edited Oct 21, 2012 5:44am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar31376_12.gif) Tw0eleven](tw0eleven)

  * | Joined Jan 2007  | Status: Feed The Piggy With Pips! | [1,772 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=31376)

**UPDATE: I don't use this method anymore, I have switched to a similiar 15minute method.**  
  
I've been learning forex for four over years now, bouncing from one system to the next, multiple timeframes, indicators, etc...I think I've finally found something that fits me as a trader and can be profitable. Maybe it will for you too. I'd also like to say that my method is nothing new, it's just a collection of little tid-bits I've picked up here and there throughout my journey.  
  
Alright, so below will be the general setup and rules. And I use the word rules loosely because they aren't hard/strict rules to follow...more like guidelines. But in an ever changing market, one has to be flexible. What we are trying to do overall is put the odds of the trade in our favor in the simplest way possible on the 4hr chart...hence the title of this thread.  
  
_**Chart setup**_  
1) I use the 4hr chart, I find it's more reliable (less noise) trading the higher timeframes...while still giving you a few good setups each week.  
2) Plot a 20 lwma in whatever color you want (I use magenta).  
3) Use a macd indicator with a histogram (I'll attach the one I found on ForexFactory at the bottom of this post). The standard settings and double them, so (24,52,18).   
  
Looking for Trades is as simple as 1-2-3...  
1) **PRICE ACTION**...basically I look to follow the current trend (higher highs & higher lows = uptrend while lower lows & lower highs = downtrend)...if the current(short term) trend matches up with the pairs overall trend...that's the best setup! Another thing with price action is just looking for simple candle patterns: engulfing, pinbar, tweezers, etc...that happen at prior support & resistance areas. lastly, just drawing in some simple trendlines and/or channels   
  
2) **MOVING AVERAGES**...you want to trade at/near the 20 moving average ....the best setup is when you get a Price Action(PA) setup and the moving average is heading in the same direction(up for longs, down for shorts).  
  
****the first version of this method had 3 moving averages on the chart...I have since modified and simplified it down to only 1...the 20lwma****  
  
3) **MACD HISTOGRAM**...you want the macd histogram to be lined up and heading in the same direction as your PA and MA. This helps me see where momentum is going along with the first two guidelines. The best setups are when the histogram is on the correct side of the zero line( above the zero line for longs and below the zero line for shorts).  
  
That's really it...it's really just 1-2-3...PA, MA, MACD HISTOGRAM. Hopefully I didn't confuse you too much so far and now lets get to some examples...  
  
_**Pairs I Use**_  
This method has been tested on GU, EU, EJ, GJ, AU, pairs...I have NOT tested it on any others. And my best results have come from GU,EU, EJ. GJ can get a bit wild at times if you can stomach big swings/drawdown(I can't, so I avoid it). AU is pretty decent, but the first three have been very reliable and I tend to trade them most often. I've been watching the UJ too...but this pair is tricky because some weeks it barely moves at all...other weeks it's great to trade!  
  
_**Money Management**_  
( word of caution...this is what works for me...please feel free to adjust your Target Prices and Stoplosses for what suits you).  
1) I set an initial emergency stop loss of 100pips in case the market does something weird like surprise news from a country or if you lose power for a while...at least you won't blow your account.   
2) My Target price is set at 75pips for pairs with higher Average Daily Ranges(GU, EJ, GJ) and 50pips for pairs with smaller ADR's(EU, AU)! I often see price run for 70-100pips or more on good setups...but right now, I'm looking for more consistent winners. This may be adjusted with further forward testing.  
3) You should exit your trade on the first candle that closes on the opposite side of your entry candle if your Target Price has not been hit. With the proper entry, your losses should be around 60pips or less.  
4) Stay away from HUGE candles...typically you want to enter on candles that are 50pips or less...give or take a few pips.  
  
As you can see, with a proper entry...my risk-reward is roughly 1:1!  
  
Attached below is the template I use for my MT4 charts.

> Hi! Thx for sharing simple system.. How long did you trade with it? What is your target (amount of pips) weekly?   
>    
>  Best regards, Noisee.
> 
> Ignored

The short answer...I look for 100pips a week as my goal. Basically 2 good trades.  
  
The longer answer...when I was first learning forex and trading, I had the usual beginners dreams...make lots of pips and lots of money. Of course that equated to lots of losses and some blown accounts. Therefore I have lowered my goals/expectations a lot and try to keep it simple and profitable because now I understand the value of keeping money in your account so you can always "trade another day." Also, the 100pips a week goal is just that...a Goal, not a "MUST MAKE" level. Some weeks I might only make 60pips or 20pips or even lose 50pips. Other weeks I might get 200pips! It all averages out in the long run. I will tell you though, if I happen to hit 200pips profit in a week I stop trading and enjoy the rest of the week off. Cheers!  
  
P.S. I almost forgot about your first question...I have been trading this particular method for a little more than 6 months now and found it to be quite successful. But you must stay disciplined and patient for the proper setups!

Hi fthingf,  
  
I have included a chart that might help explain the exit rule a little better. However, I would like to point out that the rules are more like guidelines...they are a little flexible and if you see a couple reasons to exit a trade sooner, by all means do. It's a fine line between holding trades too long and/or closing too early. Just how I like to have 3 or more reasons to get into a trade, if I start to get a few reasons that tell me to exit, I will exit too! Cheers!

Good eye fthingf! I was using that chart just as an example of exiting a losing trade, didn't even notice that you could go short there! You are correct. It's a great looking bearish engulfing candle that tried to push above the 20ma but ultimately closed below...With the overall down trend & ma's crossed down & macd histogram sloping down(barely).  
  
Side note: I went back and looked at the chart again on MT4, you can't really see it on the chart I posted, but that short candle setup...the actual candle is 68pips big...add a 3pip spread and you are looking at a possible loss of 70pips or more. That is getting near my upper limit of comfort. The best trades are with candles that are 50pips or less...this helps keep our money management in line with a 1:1 risk/reward ratio.  
  
Have a good day!

Hi Justice,  
I do keep weekly records of how many trades I take each week(winners/losers) and the profit/loss for that week. Unfortunately I don't think it would be fair to post the results because I did take some experimental trades not based on the rules of this system so the data is skewd a little. Also, I think it's important that each trader keeps their own stats and makes their own opinion about this method because, I'm sure you know, you can have 5 traders looking at the same chart and you could have 5 different opinions! One more thing to note...I like to consider the trade setup guidelines(1-2-3) just as that...guidlines. They are meant to be flexible and as such, some traders will get trades that other don't. I just hope some will like this method and it will help them in their journeys.  
  
As for trading this on the daily charts...I have actually looked at the daily charts. It seems valid overall. Just a couple differences...the setups come a lot less often. AND the biggest thing, you would dramatically increase your risk because you would need a bigger stoploss and the candles would be bigger. It would require extreme patience waiting for the setups AND you'd probably have to reduce the lot size you would trade on the 4hr charts. On the positive side of things...your trading would probably be less stressful and you'd only have to check the charts once or twice a day! For me, the 4hr charts are great...but if someone wants to try the daily...I'd say go for it! To each his own. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f44d.png?v=15.1)

I thought I would post this GU chart as an example of when NOT to take a trade. Earlier I posted the EU short setup...and some people might think the GU is about to do the same thing(so they think, I might have missed the EU so I'm going to get in on the GU)...but Not So Fast my friends. Make sure you stay true to the guidelines of this method...look for the BEST setups and skip the not so good one(or ones you have doubts about). It will save your account in the long run!  
  
Wanted to add one more thing about this candle...it's 100pips big! That is pretty high risk, as previously mentioned...I prefer candles around 50pips or less. I occasionally will enter on a bigger candle if the conditions look GREAT and if price is about 1/3rd to 1/2 of the way into the candle to reduce the risk.

> Hi Two, Nice thread. On this particular trade where was stop placement....above the 4hr pin ? Thanks,Tex
> 
> Ignored

Hi Tex, I always set an emergency stop loss 200pips above/below my entry price. That's in case some wild happens you protect your account from disater should it strike. Assuming you aren't tradin too heavy to begin with or over leveraging yourself! But that's the only stop loss I set...after I enter a trade, then I just check each candle close after that(every 4hr hours...gives you free time to do other things)...if price closes above/below the candle you entered on...then you just MANUALLY exit for whatever the loss is...typically 50pips or less. In this example, the top of the entry candle was 1.3778, so if you can any of the candles after your entry candle close above 1.3778, you would have closed at that level. So in this instance your entry was at 1.3739 and lets saw the next candle might have closed at 1.3800...you would have lost 61pips + spread.  
  
On the flip side...after setting the emergency stoploss I set a 50pip target price. So when you come back every 4hrs to check the charts you either 1) have reached your Target 2) have a candle that closed against you so you exit manually or 3) neither of the above occur and you just evaluate if the entry rules still apply and stay in the trade another 4hrs. But if the entry rules changed(say the ma's turned against you) then you exit for a small profit/loss. In the EU example, it would have taken 3 candles to reach 50pips profit!   
  
Side note...this trade is near the upper limit of what I feel my risk should be...you were risking 60pips or so for a 50pip reward...that's just under a 1:1 risk/reward. You never want to get more than 2:1 risk/reward.   
  
Hope that helps Tex!

  * Mar 19, 2010 9:06pm  Mar 19, 2010 9:06pm

> [Quoting fthingf](/thread/post/3565832#post3565832 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi Tw0eleven, talking about emergency stop loss I do need some advice. What if you've entered a trade but you know you can't sit in front of the computer to monitor the trade when the next 4hr signal comes?  
>    
>  Do you leave the 200 pips emergency stop in place until you can check price again, or would you tighten the stop before you leave your PC? Thanks.
> 
> Ignored

  
I want to make sure I understand your question correctly...are you asking me what happens when the next 4hr "Candle" closes or the next "4hr signal comes" as you stated?  
  
With regards to the 4hr candle close: If you can't come back to check your chars when the next 4hr candle closes...then the decision is up to you really. You can leave the emergency 200pip stop in place and just check the charts next chance you get(this is typically what happens if you feel you took a really good trade setup that fit all the guidelines). Another option would be perhaps move your stoploss from 200 to say 150 or even 100(just in case the market turns around on you...you'd be protecting your account a little more). And the last option would be to just exit the trade and take whatever profit/loss you have at that time if you won't be able to check the charts for a long period of time.   
  
With regards to what you asked me...."can't sit in front of your computer to monitor the stop before the next 4hr signal comes"...well, to be honest with you, I NEVER sit in front of my computer waiting for the next signal. I like to just check the charts for a few minutes prior to the 4hr candle close to see if anything is setting up to trade. Then, when the candle closes if there is a trade setup...I enter the trade and then walk away and check back later.  
  
Hope that helps...let me know if you have any other questions.  
  
On a side note...it's FRIDAY! I typically don't enter any trades on Friday because I like to have 3day weekends from trading. Let my mind unwind and spend time with the family. So on that note...Have a great weekend everyone!

No need to force any trades...just trade when you can.

Well everyone, you may have recalled this post where I recommended not jumping into the trade. And while price did continue down(as you can see by the chart posted below)...I wouldn't call myself wrong. Instead, I hope you guys see things in a different perspective. I wouldn't call it wrong to skip this trade, wasn't scared, wasn't nervous...instead, think of it as being Cautious and Reducing Risk. Afterall, you are trading to make money right? Not lose it!   
  
Now some may disagree with what I said above...but this is how I think of it. If I would have jumped in this trade and won, then what about the next trade that comes along like this...what if I jump in that one and take a loss? Then another one comes along and I say, "well, I have a 50/50 win/loss ratio so far on these trades...maybe I'll try one more." Oops, another loss! Well my friends, you just lost 2 out of 3 trades because you took trades that really weren't that good in the first place. And now you might be pissed at yourself or the market or worst yet, you think this method is flawed and doesn't work. That's definitely not good for the mental aspect of trading.  
  
So what's the worst that can happen if you skip the trade? Well, you missed out on 50pips...your account balance is the same and you are just looking for the next trade. I really don't see much wrong with this option. If truly believe it's the successful traders who pick this option!   
  
Hope everyone is having a good weekend so far!

Good chart and Good eye my friend! Everything you mentioned above I agree with and it would have been a nice entry candle if it wasn't greater than 80pips. As for it being friday...I just personally don't like to trade on Friday but that doesn't mean you can't trade it! ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1) To be honest, I have seen some Friday candles that work out great(you might have to hold over the weekend though). One of my reasons for not trading on Friday is that in my experience I never know if the trends will continue or if traders will stop trading(lose momentum) getting ready for the weekend or if traders will take profits and the trend will reverse. But again, that's just me...and I also like 3 days weekends(from tradin)! haha  
  
One more thing...I do have a second setup on the 4hr method that I have been holding off on because I wanted to see how many people were interested in trading this method and getting the first setup down before introducin the second. However, it seems that you are doing pretty well with the first so I will explain the second.  
  
We will use the same chart of GU from friday. You correctly pointed out the bearish engulfing candle along with 5/20 crossing down and macd histogram sloping down...Only problem, the entry candle was too big. How do you solve that? Well, you wait for a pullback at/near the 5/20 ma's!!! In this case, the next candle, as you can see, pulled back to the 5ma(1.5188) which was very close to the 20ma. That's where you would have gone short. This would greatly reduce your risk should the trade end up going against you! Also, you have a couple things workin in your favor: 1) the price would have to reverse against the currnet trend which isn't always easy 2) price would have to fight it's way back through the Movings Averages, also not always easy to do and 3) Since you are trading the 4hr charts, it usually takes a while for macd to turn around...another not so easy thing to do.   
  
So in this example: you would have went short on the pullback oof the candles AFTER the bearish engulfing one with your entry approximately 1.5180ish. The top of the Bearish engulfing candle was 1.5153...thus giving you an approximate risk of about 80pips if the candle closed against you. That's within my personal limit of 2:1 risk/reward.   
  
Side note: Personally, on GU I like to look at a few key areas for price to stall at, the 00's, 20's, 50's, 80's(ex: 1.5200, 1.5220, 1.5250, 1.5280). With EU and EJ I mainly look at the 00's and 50's. Also, if you are going to use this second entry method...you will need to be available to look at your charts since you'll never know exactly when price is goint pullback for your entry. If your platform allows it, you can also set alarms that way you are still able to do things around the house without having to be glued to the computer screen.  
  
I know I just gave a lot of information...if any of it needs clarification, please let me know. Cheers!

211, I actually only trade pullbacks. unfortunately, this keeps me from taking certain types of trades. and i only get a hand full of trades per week on the h4, but, they are usually good. A couple of these usually occur when i'm asleep. Teaching yourself to go long when the market has seemingly reversed and starting to look short can be cause for consternation. however, it greatly reduces the risk.

Hi Jack Daniel,  
  
To be honest, I've never traded this method on the USDCHF pair. So I'm not sure how well it works on that pair. But as far as your analysis...it looks pretty good. You had a nice bearish engulfing candles where price touched/bounced off the 200ma. And the 5/20ma crossed down AND you spotted Divergence on the macd histogram. So nice work on that. However, there are a couple things that stick out to me: 1) that bearish engulfing candle is nearly 100pips big...so right away you are risking a lot on that trade...I hope you traded a little lighter than normal. 2) price is technically still trending up because it's making HigherHighs and HigherLows...so you'll want to watch this carefully. Perhaps draw a trendline in there.   
  
All in all...not a bad trade. I just see a couple things that could cause price to go up as well as down. So just keep monitorin it...if price closes back above the ma's and/or the ma's cross back up and/or macd starts going higher again...perhaps get out of the trade? Goodluck and thanks for posting your chart!

> [Quoting TheGreatMilenko](/thread/post/3574574#post3574574 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I apologise if this question has already been answered, but what do you use the 200ema for?
> 
> Ignored

Good question, no one has asked it so far. I basically keep the 200ema on my charts to see possible turning points on price action. I can't recall off the top of my head exactly, but I believe the 200ma was voted the most useful indicator in forex. Gives a good idea of which way price is trending overall. Also, you'll see a lot of times price likes to go up to and touch or get close to the 200 only to be rejected pretty well. Could help you look to get into a trade if you see the other entry criteria as well. Also, if I see price hanging around the 200ma...and/or the 5&20 ma going up and down around the 200...i tend to stay away from the market because it's usually choppy. I like to see price moving away from the 200 usually meaning we are getting into a trend again...which is very helpful and profitable with this method.  
  
Hope that clears up things and let me know if you have any more questions. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

You know, when I first read about your strategy, the "scary" part was about money management - target 50 pips but with an emergency stop of 200 pips and manual exit upon a candle in the opposite direction. Yet this is also pretty innovative and is something which I haven't quite heard about before.  
  
I can see the advantages of this exit method - avoid being stopped out prematurely because of market noise or stop hunting.  
  
Now after reading the above comments you made in post #31, it appears to me that this strategy is not so scary after all. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1)

Yes, the 200pip emergency stoploss is scary to most. But imho, it rarely gets hit if you 1) follow the guidelines of this system and 2) definitely don't trade during major news releases like NonFarmPayroll or Interest Rates, etc... If you see you entered a bad trade or get out of a good trade when it goes against you, then your actual loss is typically 50pips or less. Cheers!

fthingf,  
  
that's normally what i do, i wait for the next bar to pull back to the ma's, i use 21, but no biggie. it appears to do it most of the time. if it doesn't, the move is suspect to me.  
  
it also minimizes the risk when i exit on the close on the wrong side. here again, if it doesn't break the low of the close on the wrong side, i exit on the touch of the ma's and if it looks like a reversal, i'll reverse.  
  
Scottie

Hi Scottie, just want to clarify your points.   
  

> [Quoting Scottie](/thread/post/3580025#post3580025 "View Quoted Post")

> Disliked

> fthingf,  
>    
>  that's normally what i do, i wait for the next bar to pull back to the ma's, i use 21, but no biggie. it appears to do it most of the time. if it doesn't, the move is suspect to me.
> 
> Ignored

Are you referring to entry here? I'm assuming that once there's an entry signal, you'll not enter at the opening price of the next candle, but wait for price to pull back to the 21 first?  
  

> Quote
> 
> Disliked
> 
> it also minimizes the risk when i exit on the close on the wrong side. here again, if it doesn't break the low of the close on the wrong side, i exit on the touch of the ma's and if it looks like a reversal, i'll reverse.

  
Do you mean when there's an exit signal, you'll again wait for price to pull back to the 21 instead of closing right away? Thanks.

Well, definitely nothing wrong with skipping a trade(can't hurt your account). It's a shame MACD was sloping down or it would have been a Great Setup! Here's one of those situations where some traders would take the trade and some skip it...and that's my main reason for not posting any results on my account! My account means nothing to all other traders because we all take/skip trades for our own reasons.  
  
I also agree with you skipping entering the trade after the big bullish candle...way too much risk! Not until a trader gets REALLY comfortable with their trading style and method should you consider taking trades on bigger candles...and IF you do, at a smaller lot size.   
  
Keep up the good work fthingf...seems like you are doing great! I hope we get some more traders like you in here so we can have more discussions. Also hope we get some good action next week since this week was REALLy slow! ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

Well, the trades don't get much better than this! Not only did we have our 1-2-3 guidelines met...there were some bonus reasons for this long trade on EU. So lets go over them:  
1) PA gave us a pinbar  
2) 5/20 ma had just crossed  
3) Macd histogram was sloping up  
4) Macd Histo was also going above the zero line(makes the trade that much better)  
5) Macd moving average lines(Number 4 in the chart) were crossing up...another bonus  
6) You can see 2 trendlines I drew(yellow lines) were broken to the upside  
7) We opened this week with a Gap that filled nicely down to the 20ma and got rejected to form our pinbar.  
  
How many more reasons do you need to go long???? ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f601.png?v=15.1)

Welcome aboard Forest-Sea!  
  
I'm sure fthingf will have to answer your first question...but I'm guessing he entered right when the candle closed to form the PB(pinbar) since there was no signal prior to that. In my opinion, since the PB candle was only 30pips big, I would have entered right away and NOT waited for the pullback. However, if the PB candle was bigger than 50-60pips...waiting for price to pullback would be the better option in order to reduce your risk on the trade.(and a side note...if price didn't pullback for you...then OH WELL...you missed a trade and move on to the next).  
  
As for your second question. Sometimes there are more than 2 setups a week...maybe 4,5,6 on a really good week. The choice is up to you on how much you trade. Personally, my goal is about 100pips a week. Sometimes I get it, sometimes I don't. I do place a limit on myself...if I ever reach 200pips(and I have on occasion)...I stop trading for the week and take some extra time off! I think it's important not to overtrade and take some time to yourself away from the chart to go do some fun things!   
  
Let me know if you have any more questions and hope you enjoy the h4 method! Please post some charts some time. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

Hi Forest,  
  
Personally, I do prefer to look for 3 main candle patterns(PA). 1) Pinbar 2) Engulfing Candle or 3) Tweezers/RailRoad Tracks. There are a lot of other candle patterns out there...but I find these the most useful. Of course you can trade anything you want...however, I try to put the odds in my favor of a successful trade. That's why I look for the 1-2-3 guidelines to line up before entering. If you have some other things that you have experienced as a trader and they are consistantly profitable for you...by all means use them! The main thing we want is High Probability Trades with Minimum Risk! 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#73](/thread/post/3596589#post3596589 "Post Permalink")

  * Mar 31, 2010 12:02am  Mar 31, 2010 12:02am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar31376_12.gif) Tw0eleven](tw0eleven)

  * | Joined Jan 2007  | Status: Feed The Piggy With Pips! | [1,772 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=31376)

> [Quoting fthingf](/thread/post/3596358#post3596358 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi Forest-Sea, I personally do not track U/CAD but I'll try to offer my view. I would have taken short at one of the candles highlighted in below chart, as to me they are bearish pin bars (although small ones). Both pins cannot close above the 20ema (and actually the top of the candle are confined by the 20 as well).  
>    
>  On the other hand I notice that the ascending trendline starting form Mar 17 has just been broken, adding to my confidence to go short.  
>    
>  As Tw0eleven has said, take the trades that you can find multiple reasons to support your view....
> 
> Ignored

  
Forest, I'd have to agree with with fthingf said above. Get the odds in your favor...multiple reasons for shorts. Also, look at the other side of things...what reasons do you have to go long??? As long as the list for shorts is bigger than the list for longs...and the PA, MA's, MACD all line up...that's your best chance at a winning trade. I don't usually trade U/Cad, but I do have the chart up just to watch.   
  
One more thing...typically GU, EJ, GJ are good moving pairs...they move over 100pips a day on average. While EU, AU, UCAD are typically lower. Initially I mentioned setting a 50pip target price on all the pairs. But with EU, AU, UCAD if you change that to 30pips and your success rate will go up a lot more. Just remember since you are only taking 30pips profit you want to make sure your entry only has an initial risk around 50pips or less otherwise the moneymanagement aspect goes out the window!  
  
Cheers! 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

Thank you, again, for sharing your earned wisdom and experience.

  * [#75](/thread/post/3596676#post3596676 "Post Permalink")

  * Mar 31, 2010 12:17am  Mar 31, 2010 12:17am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar31376_12.gif) Tw0eleven](tw0eleven)

  * | Joined Jan 2007  | Status: Feed The Piggy With Pips! | [1,772 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=31376)

I have just been looking and toying with the idea of possibly letting trades run a little longer instead of taking the standard 50pip profit target. The idea is simple...once you find a trade to enter into, let the trade run until price closes opposite side of the 5ma that you entered on. Examples will be shown below.  
  
***The risk on this though(besides the fact I have tested it....just been looking over the charts)...you could miss out on some good 50pip trades or see your profitable trades turn into breakeven or even small loss trades. For now, it's just an idea I'm throwing out there and if anyone has input...please let me know****  
  
  
there could be a lot of variations on this...such as taking a max profit of 150pips. Or if you make it to 50pips profit, move your stoploss to breakeven and just let the trade run. Or at 50pips profit set your s/l to -50 so you don't have any more than a 50pip loss...and when you reach 100pips profit move stoploss to breakeven. Guess it would be up to each individual trader.  
  
I'll be looking forward to some feedback! Happy Trading!

> [Quoting Forest-Sea](/thread/post/3596939#post3596939 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> and we would need to wait for a close of bar following the EU retrace (if it comes)?
> 
> Ignored

Nope, basically if eu retraces to 1.3440-50 area that would give you about 50pips risk(top of the big bearish candle). Your entry should be around 20ma. That way, one of two things will happen: 1) price will stay belo the 20ma and continue down thus giving you profit or 2) price will go back above the 20ma and close above...thus you exit for a smaller loss than if you entered down around 1.3400-20.  
  
Wanted to add that you don't always get a retest/touch of the ma to the exact pip...sometimes it will stop 10-15pips shy...so set an alarm(if you aren't watching the charts) for about 15-20pips prior to the ma...then you can watch PA for a little bit and see if price is stalling before the ma and you want to enter.

  * [#90](/thread/post/3597814#post3597814 "Post Permalink")

  * Mar 31, 2010 9:39am  Mar 31, 2010 9:39am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar31376_12.gif) Tw0eleven](tw0eleven)

  * | Joined Jan 2007  | Status: Feed The Piggy With Pips! | [1,772 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=31376)

> [Quoting Olu](/thread/post/3597699#post3597699 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Guys   
>    
>  I saw some analysis where trades were taken without the participation of the 200ema. Why are we plotting it on the charts? I thought it was an extra confirmation of the trend and that trades are taken only in the direction of the 200ema?  
>    
>  Clarification please...
> 
> Ignored

Hi Olu,  
  
Welcome to the thread and asking your question! the 200ema is a good indication of the Overall trend direction...but if you look back at the charts...price doesn't hang out around the 200ema for that long. It's sorta like a magnet...price moves above&below it. Price moves in cycles and we are just trying to catch some of the pips along the way. Typically it's best to trade is with the overall trend...but say the trend is down and price is way below the 200ma by about 500pips...if you get a signal to go long(countertrend...against the 200ma) that it's typically ok to take it because there is plenty of room to move up towards the 200ma. What you want to avoid is trading when price is bouncing up&down at the 200ma(moving sideways in a range).   
  
The 5 and 20 moving averages are our main signals to trade...and the 200 is just like a guide to help point us in the right direction. I hope that helps...and if I can clarify something else please let me know.  
  
Hope you enjoy this thread! 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

> [Quoting fthingf](/thread/post/3598241#post3598241 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Great for you!  
>    
>  I myself am a bit more conservative, so I wait for the last 4hr candle to close which is a bearish engulfing. I entered short at 1.3395.  
>    
>  Seeing that yesterday's daily candle is a bearish engulfing as well, I'll aim for 50 pips for this trade.
> 
> Ignored

Techinically, I think the more conservative thing to do is enter on the pullback to the MAs...that way there is less risk on your trade. If you enter on candle close when price is further away from the ma's, that means the more room price has to move against you before hitting any suppor/resistance. this is especially true on engulfing candles since price closes at the highs on bullish candles and at the lows for bearish ones.   
  
As for the eu trade...I hope you exited on the close of the 0400gmt candle close(1.3432) since price closed above the 5ma AND the 5ma started turning back up AND macd started going higher again. Also that candle makes 4 candles in a row that couldn't close below the big bearish candle from yesterday at 1200gmt. Price spent 16hrs trying to go below/close below 1.3394 and couldn't so it formed a pretty solid base(support area) around that level.

A missed trade in the usdchf turned out to be a blessing after all because I would have gunned for 50pips. 

If you think you can or cannot do it you are correct

  * [#100](/thread/post/3599732#post3599732 "Post Permalink")

  * Mar 31, 2010 10:13pm  Mar 31, 2010 10:13pm 

  * [ Scottie](scottie)

  * | Joined Dec 2007  | Status: Trader | [58 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=56659)

the reason i posted the trade was to demonstrate how difficult it is to take these entries.  
  
most people that look at my entries at the same time i take them freak out. these entries come from several years of experience and observation. It works for me, but that doesn't mean a new trader could take what i do and immediately make money with it. this one turned out to be quick, but i took one earlier in the week that i was in for 8ish hours that can be a painful wait for those of you who who are used to trading shorter time frames.  
  
my target on the trade was above the bottom of the large bottom candle for a reason as well. The bottoms of those candles can turn into support as was the case last night. i didn't know that it would, i just knew that it could. in addition, this is nfp week and traditionally, when i used to go for a runner on nfp, i'd get torpedoed.  
  
Scottie

I think you're doing great fthingf...really picking up how this method works! To be honest, even if you waited for a pullback on eu(after the engufling candle) and entered it still would have been a loss. I'll be the first to admit this method is NOT 100% winners. We just try to pick the best setups we can and then it's up to the market to decide where it goes. As with learning any new way to trade, it takes time. The best thing I have seen from the trades you have posted is that you are taking small losses(less than 50pips)!!! A lot of traders don't know how to do that and end up taking HUGE losses thinkin the market will turn in their favor if they just hold on a little longer. Keep up the good work!

Olu, my best advice on Taking profits...get to know what the average daily ranges are for the pairs you trade. And then typically go for about half of that for your profits. Say for example the GU puts in 100pip range each day...only look for 50pips profit. I mean honestly, how often can a trader(professional or not) enter the market at the exact perfect Low or High of a trade and exit at the exact High or Low and capure ALL 100pips of the move??? You might get lucky once in a while...but I don't like trading on luck...I might as well go to Las Vegas and try my luck there too! This advice is for everyone...use realistic goals! Happy trading!  
  
211

Better to have missed a trade than take a loser right? ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1) And I just want everyone to keep in mind that you can NOT be focused on exact price levels when waiting for entry points. Take the EU last night for example...if you are waiting for it to pullback to 1.3440, remember price could stop 10-15pips prior. I recommend setting some type of alarm that will alert you to start watching the charts when price comes within 10-20pips of where you want to enter. One more thing, the moving averages will move after each candle close...so what might have been the 1.3440 area on EU last night, after a couple candle closes it could now be at 1.3430(so you might want to start watching the charts around 1.3420ish). Happy Trading!  
  
211

Well, some people got the EU short last night for 30pips...unless you were trying for 50, then you most likely took a loss.   
  
However, it's interesting to see that after the short signal...we got a long signal right afterwards. For those of your familiar with Tweezers(also known as railroad track pattern)...here's what I see that would have been a nice profitable. Unfortunately I was sleeping when this setup, so I didn't take it. But it's a great example to look at!  
  
***side note****the only think that would make me think twice about this trade is that price closed below the 20ma, instead of above it...so I might have waited to see it go above before entering.

  * [#107](/thread/post/3600413#post3600413 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 1, 2010 1:43am  Apr 1, 2010 1:43am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar114404_1.gif) Forest-Sea](forest-sea)

  * | Joined Aug 2009  | Status: Trader | [561 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=114404)

Friends,   
  
Clearly if we are going to wait for a retrace prior to an entry, we can take the entry on a (near) touch of the MAs.  
  
However, if one is just entering on a 'clear' 1-2-3 set-up should we move into the position at a bar close or when it all appears.   
  
For instance, if we are mid-four hour candle and we see a pin bar developing coupled with a recent MA cross and correctly moving MACD bars, would you take entry then? Of course, the pin bar could go away by the end of the candle, but, then again, it could continue up to a TP?  
  
Whither go we? ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1) What is the optimal protocol?  
  
Forest 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#108](/thread/post/3600474#post3600474 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 1, 2010 2:08am  Apr 1, 2010 2:08am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar31376_12.gif) Tw0eleven](tw0eleven)

  * | Joined Jan 2007  | Status: Feed The Piggy With Pips! | [1,772 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=31376)

> [Quoting Forest-Sea](/thread/post/3600413#post3600413 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Friends,   
>    
>  Clearly if we are going to wait for a retrace prior to an entry, we can take the entry on a (near) touch of the MAs.  
>    
>  However, if one is just entering on a 'clear' 1-2-3 set-up should we move into the position at a bar close or when it all appears.   
>    
>  For instance, if we are mid-four hour candle and we see a pin bar developing coupled with a recent MA cross and correctly moving MACD bars, would you take entry then? Of course, the pin bar could go away by the end of the candle, but, then again, it could continue up to a TP?  
>    
>  Whither...
> 
> Ignored

  
For me, I MUST wait for candle close to get the Pinbar, Engulfing candle, Tweezers, etc... AFTER I get one of those patterns and confirm that the MA's are crossing and MACD agrees...then I decide if I should enter right away(candle close) OR if I need to wait for a pullback. And that decision comes from 1) Risk..is my risk greater than 50pips...then i should probably wait for a pullback. 2) Also, engulfing candles "typically" give pullbacks...so you reduce risk by waiting for a pullback if price isn't close t the ma's.  
  
Hope that helps! You must be flexible in this market.   
  
211

> [Quoting forex4me](/thread/post/3604550#post3604550 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi,

>    
>  Thanks
> 
> Ignored

Hi forex4me,  
  
The macd histogram is the Purple lines in the macd indicator...while the red&blue lines are the macd moving average lines I talk about.   
  
As for the ema's...sometime I will take a trade just as the ema's are about to cross if there is a good angle on the 5ema. I won't do it too early, but once you study the charts and get a feel for things...you will be able to tell usually when you are 1 candle away from the 5/20 emas just about to completely cross. Hope that helps!  
  
211

  * [#121](/thread/post/3608140#post3608140 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 5, 2010 4:33am  Apr 5, 2010 4:33am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar31376_12.gif) Tw0eleven](tw0eleven)

  * | Joined Jan 2007  | Status: Feed The Piggy With Pips! | [1,772 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=31376)

> [Quoting Brb-Fraudin](/thread/post/3604556#post3604556 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Nice thread OP. But shouldn't you make the same rules for exit?? So you can get more pips? Taking 30-40 pips out of 4 Hr trend is very low reward. You can check about volataility exit using ATR or you can exit on 5/20 MA cross. But very good entry indeed.
> 
> Ignored

  
I have asked myself the same question Brb-Fraudin. Basically it comes down to this...if you want more pips out of a trade(say 200-400pip winners) that means your winning percentage usually drops. But if I take smaller winners, my winning percentage went up. This is where each trader has to figure out what's best for him. Personally, I'm rather happy with 100pips a week profit on average. Some people may perfer making more...and that's fine too. To each his own! Cheers!  
  
Also, go back and check out my Post #75...it talks about this very subject.  
211

> [Quoting unclek6](/thread/post/3607443#post3607443 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> TW,   
>  thanks for bringing it back down to KISS. I think patience is the key. One signal a day or two in any pair is good for me.
> 
> Ignored

  
That's exactly how I feel...and while it might not be for everyone, I hope to find some other traders that enjoy keeping it fairly simple and not having to stare at the charts all day. Honestly, if you run the numbers...just 2 winning trades a week(100pips) trading 1 standard lot = $4000 a month! I know there's a lot of job out there that you can't make that working 40hrs/week!!! But YOU HAVE TO BE PATIENT FOR THE GOOD SETUPS/TRADES!!!! If it doesn't look good, skip it!

In reference to my post above #128 and the EU...I was originally looking for a possible long setup, however...I also said to be careful for the possible Head&Shoulders for shorts...it looks like shorts prevailed. There were a couple PB's that tried to get above the 5&20 ma's, but could never close above them. I had to work my dayjob earlier this week, so I missed it...but hopefully some of you were able to get it! GU and GJ might be getting ready for shorts...they both have 1)bearish engulfing candles 2) 5/20 ma's crossed down and 3) macd histograms sloping down AND going below the zero line! Be smart with your entries if you decide to take any of these trades...wait for pullbacks and limit your risk!!!  
  
Happy Trading, 211

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar80573_5.gif) Rastaman](rastaman)

  * Joined Sep 2008 | Status: Trader | [2,298 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=80573)

Yeah, this is close to James 16 core system.  
  
I am also using a similar system on H4 but with a few different settings.  
  
Basically 10,25,150 & 365 EMA with the new version of MACD 12,26,9, just PA and S&R using the MA.  
  
Actually, I recently came across a decent EMA crossover alert and also a NMACD with an alert. Saves you having to eyeball the chart too much.  
  
  
Maybe some of you guys will find them useful.  
  
You can turn the alerts off in both indicators. 

Attached File(s)

![File Type: mq4](https://assets.faireconomy.media/images/attach/mq4.gif) [MACD_ColorHist_AlertEMA.mq4](/attachment/file/458425?d=1271318001) 5 KB | 329 downloads 

![File Type: mq4](https://assets.faireconomy.media/images/attach/mq4.gif) [CrossedAlerts.mq4](/attachment/file/458426?d=1271318001) 2 KB | 287 downloads

I think there are 2 things here: 1) this method doesn't deal with trading Inside Bars...personally, I don't find them consistant enough to trade. 2) I would much prefer entering at/near the Moving Averages instead of waiting for price to break the high/low of candles....in my humble opinion(and with this method) it greatly reduces your risk on a trade.   
  
Hope that helps! ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

Well, I must say I'm impressed. You are the first person to notice this...I was wondering how long I could get away with having different macd settings before somone would catch it! ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f44d.png?v=15.1) Now the secret is out. hehe  
  
I think you can use the standard settings 12, 26, 9 and be just fine. I have been using the other settings lately because they seem to smooth out the histogram and it makes it visually easier for me to see where the momentum is heading. Basically, they are 8hr chart settings...I just doubled the standard 4hr settings since MT4 doesn't have an 8hr chart.   
  
The main point about using macd imho is that you make sure you are trading with the momentum of the market. So if the histogram is heading up, momentum(prices) are going up...and vice versa for shorts!   
  
Happy Trading!

  * [#158](/thread/post/3641961#post3641961 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 15, 2010 10:50pm  Apr 15, 2010 10:50pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar80573_5.gif) Rastaman](rastaman)

  * Joined Sep 2008 | Status: Trader | [2,298 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=80573)

Yes, PPZ are S&R but a little different than the regular floor pivots.  
They are drawn as no doubt you have seen previously, at areas where price has flipped. Basically it is support that has changed to resistance and visa vi.  
  
However, I do not like to draw PPZ all over the place and it can be time consuming. I sometimes use a round number indicator but on H4, you can generally tell where a price action candle is going to stall by the highs and lows nearby.  
  
Something I am currently working on is this.  
  
Find a D1 successful Pin Bar or outside bar etc and put a line on the tail and the nose, then change down to H4 and you can find many successful price action bars around those areas. They seem to repeat and so they should as a PB is basically bouncing off resistance and hitting support which either holds or breaks. Try it out.  
  
What an interesting time frame H4 is, is it not?  
Hopefully I can learn alongside you guys.

  * [#159](/thread/post/3641997#post3641997 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 15, 2010 11:03pm  Apr 15, 2010 11:03pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar80573_5.gif) Rastaman](rastaman)

  * Joined Sep 2008 | Status: Trader | [2,298 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=80573)

I am sure everyone knows there is nothing mysterious about pin bars.  
  
They are simply a Head and shoulders pattern if you move down a time frame.  
  
like this one on D1, on H4 it is a reverse Head and shoulders.  
  
  
  
I only mention this as I myself did not know what they were till I studied at J16.  
Actually, this is quite important if you think about it.  
  
That D1 PB was not very successful and the reason is, if you go down to H4 you see it is a R H&S which is a bullish signal, but this one is in an uptrend, we want to see a Head & Shoulders at a high not a Reverse head 7 shoulders. So, we can check a PB out like that also.

> 
> I am sure everyone knows there is nothing mysterious about pin bars.  
>    
>  They are simply a Head and shoulders pattern if you move down a time frame.  
>    
>  like this one on D1, on H4 it is a reverse Head and shoulders.  
>    
>    
>    
>  I only mention this as I myself did not know what they were till I studied at J16.  
>  Actually, this is quite important if you think about it.  
>    
>  That D1 PB was not very successful and the reason is, if you go down to H4 you see it is a R H&S which is a bullish signal, but this one is in an uptrend, we want to see a Head & Shoulders at...
> 
> Ignored

I am noticing that a lot of people are talking about TP of 30-60 pips!  
  
I also trade an M15 system where average TP is 50 pips and very often well over 100 pips.  
  
Possibly letting a trade run more and cutting the losers short with good money management is a way to extract more profit out of the H4.

Hi Rastaman, I'd just like to remind you that if you read the first post you'll see this method is exactly for taking 30-50pips only. There are multiple ways to trade forex, hence all the different methods. And this one prefers to make consistant smaller profits with a higher win percentage versus bigger profits with a lower win percentage by leaving runners.   
  
The choice is always up to the individual trader of course, but I don't recommend runners using this method. Have a good weekend!

Hi Olu,  
  
I've been pretty busy so haven't posted much. My wife and I have a new baby boy addition to our family. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)   
  
That being said, I think that chf trade was good on the candle that closed just at/below the ma's....that's where you should have entered(or at least i would have). The last candle on your chart looks like it already dropped pretty far so you would need to wait for price to come back up to the ma's and then stall and start back down if you wanted to enter short. The reason I would have picked the entry just as the ma's where crossin down and price was at/below the ma's is because not only did the 1-2-3 line up then...but look at your candles themselves, 2 great PinBar candles before the entry candle! That would add enough reasons for me to enter.  
  
On a side note, thank you for posting your chart. Also, that's another reason I haven't posted a lot on here lately...I don't want to be the one posting possible trades and calling the shots. I really wanted to put this system/method out there and have others trade it themselves. See if you like it...some will, some won't. If anyone has questions...feel free to ask and I or someone else on here will surely try to answer! ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1) I hope those of you that are trying this trading method are enjoying it and making pips!  
  
Happy Trading!

I wish I had a great way to explain macd for you, but I don't...I basically use it to see where the momentum is heading in the market.   
  
Keep up the good work,  
211

> [Quoting jackdaniel](/thread/post/3932992#post3932992 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi Tw0eleven,  
>    
>  If the last two posts showed your new strategy, i believe it's based on a 21 MA, MACD, PA and candlesticks.  
>  Could you send me the details of entry, exits, SL and TPs?   
>  The only thing that it's a bit odd is the fact that you missed some big moves with the trend and opted for small reversals. Or the last examples are not a good sample of the strategy?  
>

> Ignored

Hi Jackdaniel,  
  
For Entries: refer to the notes on the charts above...that's what you pretty much look for in the setup and then enter when price pulls back towards the 21ma...usually within 10pips is close enough(it's up to you if you want to wait for actually 21 touches or enter 15pips away...it's a flexible plan based on your own preferences).  
  
Exits: Either 1) your stoploss is hit, 2) Your profit limit is hit or 3) Price closes on the opposite side of the 21ma from which you entered...so you take a smaller loss than the hard stoploss.  
  
Stoploss: Initially set a 75pip stoploss( if you are comfortable with it or trading in a more volatile market...you could use up to 100pip stoploss).  
  
TargetPrice: For pairs that have larger daily ranges like GU, GJ, EJ use a 75pip target price(could use 100pips if you think it will go that far). For smaller range pairs like EU, AU, UCad use a 50pip target price.  
  
  
As for your last comment about missing the big moves...you have to decide what type of trader you want to be??? Do you want to be a trader who takes a few pips out of the market each week? Or do you want to be a trader who looks for the Home Run moves of 1000pips??? For me, personally, I could live on 100pips a week trading so I only look for 75-100pips on my trades...1 or 2 good trades a week and I'm happy. But another trade may prefer to get into a trade and hold that trade open for 500pips or more!!! The choice is yours my friend. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)  
  
  
p.s. another reason I look for only about 100pips a week is that the Big Huge Moves don't happen that often...maybe a couple times a year right? It took GU from January to May to go from 1.6400 area down to 1.4200 area. And then from those May Lows until August to reach 1.6000 area. About 2000pips for each move...and if you take the 5 months it took the first move down and divide that into the 2000pips(if you get in at the top and out at the bottom) then that's 400pips a month profit right? Or 100pips a week? ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

I think the above examples help reinforce that fact that you don't have to be in the market every week...there will be periods of no signals and then some weeks where there are LOTS of signals. In the end, it all averages out. Just focus on patience and waiting for the proper entries and you can be successful with this method(or pretty much any method you like)!

> [Quoting jackdaniel](/thread/post/3938114#post3938114 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> My first trade using the new version ... it's demo.
> 
> Ignored

  
Hey, I just spotted a couple things on your chart that I wanted to comment on. First, your MACD looked a bit different than mine...I see you have the same settings I do, but your macd histogram is above the zero line while mine is below...not sure why. But the slope is down which is what you are lookin for to get in if you get a short signal!   
  
Second, are you familiar with divergence??? You had a great example of it and I copied your chart and added it in there(the thicker yellow lines). If you're not too familiar with it, or for those of you reading this thread and not too familiar with it, I really like trades when you get a divergence signal. Basically, all it is is when price is still making higher highs(the thick yellow line above the candles)....and when the macd histogram is making lower highs(thick yellow line above macd)...that is Divergence. Price going one way and macd the other way. It signals that the upmove in price is losing it's momentum!   
  
*this also works for long setups...but in that case, price will be making lower lows while macd is making higher lows*

  * | Joined Jan 2007  | Status: Feed The Piggy With Pips! | [1,772 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=31376)

Hi Forest,  
  
Thanks for joining the thread. Hope you do well here. To answer your questions...I do have 8 pairs that I watch on one screen...AU, GU, EU, EG, UCad, GJ, EJ, UJ. However, I really only trade GU, EU, EJ...occaisonally the AU, Ucad or UJ. But I stay away from the GJ...the swings are a little more than I like to see. The reason I watch all those pairs is that I like to correlate them and see if there is one currency that is weaker/stronger than the others. Example....if AU, GU, EU are all going up and Ucad is going down it's a pretty safe bet the the Dollar is weak. Another example is if the EU, EG, EJ are going up while GU and GJ are staying the same or going down...it's pretty safe bet that there is Euro strength in the market.  
  
Hope that helps and if you have any more questions...feel free to ask!  
  
Happy Trading!

  * Aug 15, 2010 4:47am  Aug 15, 2010 4:47am

  * | Joined Jan 2007  | Status: Feed The Piggy With Pips! | [1,772 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=31376)

well, if I understand you correctly...correlation is NOT only with the eurusd. Since your chart is the EURJPY, you have to look at other EUR pairs AND JPY pairs. If you look at UJ and GJ, you'll those pairs are going up just like EJ. So there is JPY weakness overall...and that weakness is more than the eurusd. Now since the eurusd is weak, as is the gbpusd and audusd...that leads me to believe the USD is strong.   
  
So, we have JPY weakness and USD strentgh...what pair do you think we should trade knowing these two things??? USDJPY right? And that's how I try to use correlation. I hope I have helped answer your question.  
  
  
  
Also, if you were going to trade this EJ pair...you don't have a setup just yet. We just got price to make a Higher Low and it looks like the MACD is starting to turn back up...but we need price to close above the 20moving average and then enter on the pullback.

Hi Tw0eleven,  
  
to be honest, I havent done many trades yet, but so far it looks nice with 13 EMA. Today I took the USD/JPY trade (pic attached). Entered at 85.90 with TP of 40 pips. It went south for nearly 70 pips (however I was sleeping and therefore put a fixed TP of 40 pips and SL of 40 pips).

But since I was at work and missed the entry earlier..I have no choice but to wait until price pulls back to the 20 moving average...if I entered here, my Risk would be TOO great! Hope that helps clarify things.

  * Aug 18, 2010 1:12am  Aug 18, 2010 1:12am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar31376_12.gif) Tw0eleven](tw0eleven)

  * | Joined Jan 2007  | Status: Feed The Piggy With Pips! | [1,772 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=31376)

> [Quoting Tw0eleven](/thread/post/3951359#post3951359 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Time will tell, but this is how I look at setups in real time!
> 
> Ignored

  
Here is an update to this GU long setup trade. We got an entry on the pullback to the 20 moving average. However, the very next candle closed below the 20 ma, thus we needed to exit for a loss.   
  
There's a few important things I want to point out about this trade:   
  
1) up till now, you have seen many winning trade examples to get you use to what to look for. But I don't want to be accused of only showing you winning trades because that would not be an accurate representation of this method...there WILL be losing trades too. And here's the proof.  
  
2) We set the 100pip initial stoploss in order to give the trade room to move so we don't get stopped out prematurely. However, we do want to protect our account from some random market event that could cause a 500pip drop/rise in the market...so we MUST set some type of stop loss. This losing trade shows just that...we gave it room to move, yet still protected our account in case of some random BIG move in the market.  
  
3) There are a few people out there who think a 100pip stoploss is too big. But you have to remember, this is a 4hr chart...not a 5minutes chart!!! 4hr candles can move a lot. Your risk/reward on a trade should be roughly 1:1 or better. The 75-100pip stoploss does this...because we typically have a 75 target price. But what's even better about this method is that the 100pip stoploss HARDLY gets hit...if you are in a losing trade, you typically get an exit that is far less than 100pips just like this losing trade example! We only lost 53 pips on this trade...if our next trade is a winner of 75pips...then we come out ahead 22pips!!! And our overall goal in trading is to protect our accounts and come out with a profit right???  
  
Happy Trading!!!

THAT'S GREAT!!! I hope everyone reads your post and understands that you have to be flexible in this market! That's why I say use anywhere from a 75-100pip initial stoploss. And that while your initial target price is 50-75pips(depending on the pair)...you might want to take less pips if the market tells you too!   
  
In short, it's nice to have a set of rules...but you must also be flexible with them!!!  
  
As for other pairs I'm watching right now...I missed the EU trade/pullback for longs. However, the EJ looks good for a long trade if it pulls back to the 20ma.

> Disliked
> 
> Here is a setup in real time....
> 
> Ignored

  
A quick update...the 20ma was at 107.20, your entry would have been about 107.30 and currently EJ is at 107.80(50pips profit)...so you would move your 100pip stoploss up to breakeven right now if you want to play it safe!  
  
***Side Note*** You always have to be careful when your limits are at/near whole levels. In this case our 75pip goal puts our limit at 108.05. Price may stall before getting to that level(right now I see it reached a high of 107.91)...there would be absolutely nothing wrong with taking profits a little early. 50-60pips is always nice. You just have to ask yourself, is another 15-25pips worth the risk of taking breakeven? If you can handle that aspect of trading...leave the trade open. If you can't, exit the trade!

Hi Forest, thank you for posting on here. I was beginning to wonder where everyone went and if it was worth it to keep posting on here!   
  
To answer your question, yes...I do perfer to wait for price to close above/below the 20 and Macd to agree, then wait for the pullback to enter the trade. HOWEVER, in a few instances I will enter on candle close(not waiting for the pullback) IF price closes at/near(within 10-15pips) of the 20ma. That doesn't happen to often, but it does every now and then. The important thing is that you have at least 3 reasons(price action, 20ma, macd) to tell you to enter a trade, AND there aren't the same or more reasons not to enter the trades, AND your entry is at/near the 20ma to help reduce risk. Hope that helps...let me know if you have any more questions.   
  
Happy Trading and Have a good weekend!

Forest,  
  
i'm not sure about always, waiting for the pullback, I try to, and i know 211 does too. But I "always" wait for the pullback although i use the 21ema and 211 uses the 20 lma. The problem is occasionally, I slip and take a trade that doesn't meet the rules. the problem with not waiting is, if it works, then you think you were justified. if it doesn't, then you now think your kids wont' get to go to college. it boils down to the money management. and trading style. if you can let the runners run a bit with partials, then you probably don't have to be right so often and you can probably handle a bit higher draw down. in this system with taking pips at the set level, i think it is critical to wait for the pullback. for me, its about the psychological capital. i don't like to see big draw downs, when i know that all i would have had to do was wait for the pullback.  
  
hope this helps  
  
Scottie

I would agree with what Forest Sea said...usually late is better than early. I don't recommend making it a habit to get in late though...but if for some reason you are late, make sure you don't look for BIG winning trades/profits. If the normal goal is 75pips with an entry at/near the 20ma....then "late" entries should be 50, 40, or 25pips depending how late you are.

Actually, I have another question for 211, Scottie and all. Feel free to chip in your individual thoughts.

  * | Joined Jan 2007  | Status: Feed The Piggy With Pips! | [1,772 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=31376)

Hi Forest-Sea,  
  
To answer some of your questions...I do follow/watch 8 pairs( AU, EU, GU, EurGbp, UCad, GJ, EJ, UJ). However, as you said, I mainly just trade GU, EU and EJ. Occasionally I'll take an AU or UCad trade. But I have found that the previous three mentioned are more than enough for me(100pips/week goal). And as you mentioned, most of those pairs are correlated...so I wouldn't want to be long AU, GU, EU or short GJ, EJ, UJ all at the same time and have them go against me. Another thing is with the new margin requirements in the US it's probably not too easy to open multiple trades. The EG and UJ pairs I typically don't trade, I just use them to see how the other pairs are moving...and I find that GJ just has some pretty wild swings at times so I just stay away. Hope that helps, let me know if you have any more questions.

Two,  
  
Have you attempted to put together a win/loss ratio for the 4 Hour KISS?  
  
This is quite different from 'how many pips' or 'how much money.' Those are personal and depend on account size and the size of lots one takes at entry.  
  
I can't put an exact % on it, but it looks like no less than 70% of your entries are closed with some profit, often at your TP point.  
  
Just wondered if you could offer something a little more exact.   
  
Bottom line, no one trades any system for month after month without success. I heartily congratulate you, Andrew, for building a simple but ongoing successful system.  
  
You don't trade Fridays. Good idea not to carry positions over the weekend, of course, so enjoy your weekend and three trading days off.  
  
Best to you, Forest

Hi Forest,  
  
You are correct, I don't think this method is less than 70% win/loss...typically it's 80% or better. But like you said, it depends on the individual trader and how patient they are at waiting for the proper signals...how disciplined they are at waiting for pullbacks to enter at/near the 20ma(not getting in too early or late to trades).  
  
If you look at the trades this week just on the 3 pairs I normally trade. GU gave a short setup on Tuesday good for 75pips and both EU and EJ gave short setups Wednesday morning good for 50 and 75ipps respectively. 3 trades, all winners(100%) for a total of 200pips! But how many traders are patient enough to NOT jump into any trades on Sunday or Monday???? This method is about 95% mental discipline and chart reading. I hope you are finding success with it!

  * [ Scottie](scottie)

I'm still mental, but the success rate is good. every once in a while i do something stupid and waste some capital from my account. but this is a labour of love. i enjoy it and its starting to work. not something that takes a month of knowledge and you are there. but the success rate seems 80%. with some chart reading.  
  
211 and i have traded together for over 3 years. we watch the same pairs. our systems are almost identical. we have researched and tried many different things. one of the biggest things we came up with was to watch price action. then we discovered price action in the direction of the trend.  
  
my biggest problem is not waiting for the candle close. look at ej and eu yesterday. i had a nice short entry on both of those. what did i do? took profits early. did i need to? apparently not  
  
if i conscientiously waited for the close, i know i'd do better income wise. so that is my new goal.  
  
Wait for the close whether i'm staring at the charts or not.

I like this system very much.  
  
I have made 5 trades within one week (from Sept. 2nd until today) and all of them were winners.  
  
All 5 trades with TP between 40-50 pips and SL between 35-45 pips. Most of these trades were good for 70 pips and one trade (EJ) even for 250 pips!  
  
I always check also daily and weekly time frame and only trade when the MA of all 3 time frames move in the same direction.  
  
Thanks 211 for this great system. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

Well, I am behind 211, Scottie and fguru on the patience and mental angle so crucial to success . . . _BUT_ you are really helping me edge in the right direction.  
  
I think what I am trying to show myself is that the KISS rules followed pretty carefully do yield that 70-80% win rate. Jump in too soon, or skip one of the 1-2-3 guides and negative things _might_ happen. Of course, the counter in my mind to this is that those 'no quite qualified' entries can lead to bigger gains if you are not trading for a fixed number of pips. (I suppose this means you can and do really watch the screen during live trades)  
  
Are any of you taking multiple entries and making a fixed profit your TP1 then you keep going with a second or possibly more positions?   
  
Thanks to all and good weekend.

Hi Forest-Sea,  
  
I don't recommend taking multiple entries UNLESS you are cutting your lot size in half in order to account for 2 trades being open. Always use good money management, don't over leverage yourself or trade too big of a lot size!  
  
Now that being said, my target prices of either 50pips or 75pips depending on the pair are what I like to use. Anyone can feel free to use something else...and there have been many cases where I have seen that leaving a trade open longer, instead of taking the 75pip hard limit, would have gotten a trader 100, 200, even 500pips if the trend was strong enough! However, how often do those type of trades happen? Each trader has to figure out what type of trader they are! Can they be happy taking 10 trades where you're looking to get 50pip winners about 80% win/loss ratio??? Or can they be happy taking 10 trades where you're going for 500pips and only win about 10% of the time??? In the end, it would appear both types of traders would get 500pips...each individual just has to figure out how they want to go about it(or what they are comfortable with).   
  
Have a good weekend!

All right, I am going to watch each candle end/start for the KISS this week, including the one that rolls in the middle of my night.  
  
In looking at where we are now, it raised another question.   
  
I have been reluctant to take any trade in which the _slope_ of the LWMA 20 was not at least slightly moving in the direction of the cross and new trend.  
  
However, I am seeing that the touch or cross of the 20 will not infrequently occur PRIOR to the 20 turning (up or down).  
  
211, Scottie and all, what do you guys do in this case? Let's say the MACD bars are clearly moving in your direction and price has crossed the 20, BUT the 20 is not yet flattened out completely or turned.  
  
Good trading week to all.   
  
Forest

Forest,   
  
lets say there was an extended move down and i'd like to go long. that first touch of the 21 after the break will usually still bounce down, so i don't like to go long that soon. i wait till it retests the low and makes a higher low and higher high or closes higher than a bunch of candles above the 21. these higher lows and higher highs need to be a fractal that takes several bars to make. the pattern at that point is complete and i'll take the pullback long.  
  
Scott

Sorry for the late response, I have been traveling today. You are right, at least for me...I don't watch the AJ charts. Also, to answer your 1hr entry question...I do not enter off the 1hr chart. All my entries/exits are off the 4hr chart. HOWEVER, I do look at other timeframes(1hr, Daily, Weekly) just to get an idea of price action, the trend and where some prior support/resistance areas are.  
  
As for trades today...it was an interesting day! Speaking just about the 3 primary pairs I trade...GU was just in a range, so I basically ignored it this week. EU had a nice run up in price that started last week, had a pullback early this morning that only came within 17pips of the 20ma(so not close enough for an entry)....and EJ was tricky...you had EU going up but UJ going down so EJ was basically fighting and struggling to pick a direction. When EJ closed below the 20ma this morning MACD was still heading up, the 20ma was still at a good angle up, AND most importantly if you look at that candle that closed below the 20ma...it was a pullback to prior broken resistance area from last week on Sept. 8th and 10th...this was the FIRST retest of that area(107.00 area). So for me, I was actually thinking longs on EJ instead of shorts.   
  
Good questions you have posted...keep them coming!

Well, it would have been nice...but you have to be honest...do you get these types of moves that often???? Once every six years??? I'm more than happy taking 50-75pips each week instead of 200pips once every six years!!!

Hi tradpat,  
  
I wouldn't say I'm very disciplined, I still make my fair share of mistakes from time to time. But if you can manage to follow the rules of this system, I see no reason why you won't be profitable.  
  
As for your question about how many trades I have taken...to be honest with you, I don't have that information readily available. I keep track of how many trades(winners/losers) I have each week...but some of my trades are not based on the 4hr method but sometimes just price action alone. So if I were to give you the trades I have taken, that information could be misleading to you. Also, since this method is based on price action...and everyone reads charts a little differently, there might be some trades I would take that you would not...or trades you would take that I would now. So that could also be misleading, which I don't want to mislead anyone. I can still post my numbers if you would like, just let me know...and understand that some of my trades are not based solely on the 4hr method.

>  I wouldn't say I'm very disciplined, I still make my fair share of mistakes from time to time. But if you can manage to follow the rules of this system, I see no reason why you won't be profitable.  
>    
>  As for your question about how many trades I have taken...to be honest with you, I don't have that information readily available. I keep track of how many trades(winners/losers) I have each week...but some of my trades are not based on the 4hr method but sometimes just price action alone. So if I were to give you the trades I have taken,...
> 
> Ignored

There are a lot of EA's out there and I'm sure some of them could work...but you just can't replace the human thought process. And with this method, I don't believe you could ever use an EA...you MUST be able to reason when a trade to trade and when NOT to trade. Here are two examples, EU and EJ, where a computer EA would have most likely gotten you into a trade...but you can see with human reasoning, you would stay out of the market.

  * [#332](/thread/post/4061152#post4061152 "Post Permalink")

  * Sep 30, 2010 8:40pm  Sep 30, 2010 8:40pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar31376_12.gif) Tw0eleven](tw0eleven)

  * | Joined Jan 2007  | Status: Feed The Piggy With Pips! | [1,772 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=31376)

Well, I must admit...GU got me yesterday! I went for the short setup and it ended up being a loser. However, there was a long setup right after that that was a winner. A couple comments about these two trades I want to make clear:  
  
1) You will NOT be a winner 100% of the time with this system or any system that I'm aware of. But that doesn't mean you won't be successful!  
  
2)I want to stress that PROPER trade management and money management will keep you trading and profitable!!! Even though I use an initial 100pip stoploss(and that's just in case the market REALLY does something wild and goes against you)...most of the time you will only have a 50pip or less loss. Now if you take a 50pip or 75pip winner after that....you are already back to breakeven or in a small profit for the week!!! Think about that... you took 2 trades, 1 loss and 1 winner( A 50% win/loss ratio)...AND YOU STILL HAVE AN ACCOUNT TO TRADE WITH!!! If you just follow the 1-2-3 rules about entering a trade and you have a good idea how to read Price Action....you will be SUCCESSFUL MORE THAN 50% of the time with this method!!!

Here are a couple more examples of trades from last night/this morning:  
  
1) EU...this one was pretty simple, just follow the trend...be patient for the pullback to the 20ma and pounce on it!   
  
2) EJ...I put this example in here to show you guys/gals what your thought process should be on what to look for ENTERING trades and WHEN NOT TO Trade. Always remember, you need ALL of the 1-2-3 conditions met(price action, price in relation to the 20 moving average, and MACD) for a good, valid trade entry setup!
