  * Sep 30, 2010 8:56pm  Sep 30, 2010 8:56pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar31376_12.gif) Tw0eleven](tw0eleven)

  * | Joined Jan 2007  | Status: Feed The Piggy With Pips! | [1,772 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=31376)

Ok, first...I DON'T recommend taking all of the previous 4 trade examples I showed. In reality, there were only 2 good trades that should have been taken.  
  
HOWEVER, for those of you who are new, not the best with price action yet, and/or just made a simple mistake like I did(on that first gu short trade)....I want to stress the importance of proper discipline,trade management, money management!!!  
  
1) You MUST follow the exit rules just as you would the entry rules. Take that GU short trade setup...the exit rules state you have to exit on the first candle that closes on the opposite side of the 20ma from where you entered. So I went short GU with price below the 20ma...the first candle that closed above the 20 is where you exit. It resulted in a 40pip loss...that's a fairly small loss for a 4hr timeframe trade! Small losses keep you in the trading game!!! That's where Discipline comes in..FOLLOW THE RULES!!!  
  
2) Had you not closed when you did and made the rookie mistake of waiting for price to pullback to where you could exit at breakeven...That would NOT have happened...GU never pulledback that far. You would be down about 100pips right now...you just DOUBLED your loss by not following the rules!!! That's where Trade Management comes in...or in this case, LACK OF Trade Management because you didn't do a very good job of keeping your losses small!  
  
  
3) Now for whatever reason, lets say you took all 4 trades. GU Short for a 40pip loss, GU long for a 75pip gain, EU long for a 50pip gain, EJ long for breakeven and EJ short for breakeven. Add up all the gains/losses and you would have shown a GAIN of 85pips for the week so far!!! That's pretty good in my humble opinion for only having a 50% win/loss ratio! Had you taken the valid trade setups(GU long and EU long)...you'd be up 125pips!!! That's pretty good Money Management and that's the power of this method!!!!  
  
Trade Smart everyone!!!!

Hi WickstedFX,  
  
There are 3 main things to look at for a trade setups..First(and most important) is Price Action. Second is the 20 MA(make sure you are trading on the correct side of it...longs above it, shorts below it. And Third is Macd(just the histogram).   
  
Now to answer your question about Macd...the BEST setups are when macd is heading in your direction AND on the correct side of the zero line! Example: You want to go long...make sure Macd is heading up and above the zero line. HOWEVER...there are times when it's perfectly fine to go long when macd is heading up, but it's still below the zero line. But that will have to be your decision to make...If Price action and the 20ma are obviously telling you long is the way to go...then go with it. Just be cautious that the trade "might" not work out.

Yes, that could very well happen. Just make sure you keep an open mind because that's not the ONLY option available. Price could go down, bounce off the trendline and only go a little bit higher and then drop again(forming a lower high and possibly be the beginning of a trend reversal). Also, price may not go down that far to bounce off the trendline. I guess my point is, be patient...let price action develop and tell you what it's going to do. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)  
  
Also, I have attached your chart below...what you said above could happen. Also, another thing to look out for is prior support&resistance areas! The Red circles are where there was prior resistance that has been broken...and you can see that a couple of times price has retraced back down to those prior areas(RED LINES). If you get the correct price action, 20ma touch, macd signals AND price reaches a prior suppor/resistance area, that makes your trade a higher probability of success! ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)  
  
Trade Smart!

With regards to my above post...EU just did the same exact thing I was talking about! It pulled back at/near the 20ma(within 15pips) AND it was also a pullback to prior resistance area that seems to have turned into support!!! One very important aspect of these trades is that if you have a trade setup, you want it to be the FIRST or maybe second retest of these areas. After that, your probability of a successfull trade really goes down.

>    
>  Cheers
> 
> Ignored

Entries don't often come at candle closes...they typically happen while the candle is forming( the pullback to the 20ma ). Now if the candle had closed at/near the 20ma...then you might have an entry at candle close if price action looked good enough. Hope that helps.  
  
p.s. if you wait until candle close for entries, you typically miss most of the move!

  * [#353](/thread/post/4086063#post4086063 "Post Permalink")

  * Oct 11, 2010 3:46am  Oct 11, 2010 3:46am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar31376_12.gif) Tw0eleven](tw0eleven)

  * | Joined Jan 2007  | Status: Feed The Piggy With Pips! | [1,772 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=31376)

I am going over the charts from last week before trading starts this week and I came across this. This is a great example of how to use support and resistance areas to your advantage. This is the AU 4hr chart and you can see there was an area of resistance around .9700 the last week of Sept. Price finally broke through that area on Oct. 6th. Once that area is broken, it typically turns into support....just like it did on Oct. 8th! Those are some of my favorite type of setups when it lines up with the rest of the rules of this 4hr method.   
  
One other note, the highest probability trades are FIRST TOUCH trades. What I mean by that is the first time price goes back to retest a prior Support or Resistance area. OR whenever price touches the 20 moving average for the first time after a trend change. Each touch after that becomes less and less probable of a successful trade.  
  
Goodluck this week and Trade Smart!

  * Oct 11, 2010 9:25pm  Oct 11, 2010 9:25pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar31376_12.gif) Tw0eleven](tw0eleven)

  * | Joined Jan 2007  | Status: Feed The Piggy With Pips! | [1,772 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=31376)

> [Quoting freedomsg](/thread/post/4087347#post4087347 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi 211, EJ 4 hr slowing diverenge. Price is up but MACD sloping down.. how will you play this setup? Thanks
> 
> Ignored

This is a somewhat tricky setup. Overall, it seems like we are in an uptrend AND MACD is above the zero line. However, in the short term(last few days)...price has been making Lower Highs and Lower Lows. Price is below the 20ma, we had a trendline/channel break to the down side and MACD divergence with MACD sloping down.   
  
So with all that being said, I wouldn't be going long until price stops making new lows. So shorts are the way to go for now, just be careful and look left at prior support/resistance areas where price may stop. You could take profit sooner than the normal 75pip target. Also, since it's not the best setup, you could be conservative and move your stoploss up to break even at +40 to +45pips.   
  
Also, you could be REAL conservative and not take any trades at all until a better setup comes along. You have to decide what risk you can/cannot take and be satisfied with. I hope that helps.  
  
Trade Smart! ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

Hi Forest,  
  
I use 1mini lot per $2000 in my account. Example, if I had $20,000 in my account I would be trading 1 standard lot. It's a bit aggressive, if you use the standard 100pip stoploss...1 loss would be 5% of your account. I'm ok with that since I'm so use to and experienced with this method. But it's not for everyone!!!  
  
For any new traders I would recommend demo trading first OR for those who don't like demo trading...go with something like 1mini per $5000. Or if you want to be REALLY conservative, go with 1mini per $10,000 in your account. The choice is up to each trader and what they are personally comfortabl with.  
  
Just remember, TRADE SMART!!!

  * Edited 1:50am  Oct 17, 2010 1:48am | Edited 1:50am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar114404_1.gif) Forest-Sea](forest-sea)

  * | Joined Aug 2009  | Status: Trader | [561 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=114404)

> [Quoting Tw0eleven](/thread/post/4100215#post4100215 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I'm ok with that since I'm so use to and experienced with this method. But it's not for everyone!!!  
>    
>  TRADE SMART!!!
> 
> Ignored

  
Actually, I think this is an excellent answer. You are very comfortable, and successful, with this approach and understand that, over time, you have a positive expected value (gain) per trade. As long as the EV is positive the strong argument is to bump up the risk since the reward is essentially known (maybe not on this trade but over a basket of trades, yes).  
  
And, truthfully, many would see that 5% as near the top of a trade risk, but acceptable.   
  
I'm not ready to go there, BUT I am glad to know that this kind of trading is very possible.   
  
BTW, what program do you use to annotate your charts for posting?  
  
Best, Forest

I typically don't post trades ahead of time because I want each trader to learn how to recognize trade setups and trade for themselves....I don't want to be a "signal caller." But, in this case I thought I would help out some new traders to give some insight in my thought process on what I look for before a trade happens....which is basically the same as all my other examples. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)  
  
Whether these trades actually materialize or not is up to the market...but I know what I'm looking for now and where price needs to go in order to enter.

Hi Forest,   
  
You know, I was thinking the same thing on AU...but I don't usually trade it, so I didn't mention it. I left it up to you guys! haha Also, I try not to get myself into too many trades at one time...especially is they are all tied together(like AU, EU, GU all are based on the dollar...so you could have 3 losing trades if the dollar is weak and you went short those three pairs). That's another reason I try to stick with EU, GU and EJ.  
  
But regarding AU, I don't see a setup just yet. However, it looks like it's making a Lower High...so shorts could be on the table in the next candle or two.   
  
Trade Smart!

> [Quoting freedomsg](/thread/post/4106528#post4106528 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi 211, I took this trade few hours ago. The white arrow show a short term bearlish Harami and two candles later was a bearlish engulfment (orange arrow). I should have wait till it retrace back to the 20 ma (lesson learn). I short at the next candle open after the bearlish engulfment. My question is the exit... how do u place it? I tp 10 pips before the red line. Am i doing it wrongly... thanks and cheers ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f44d.png?v=15.1)
> 
> Ignored

  
Hi Freedom,   
  
It appears that you are using a slightly different method than what I show on this thread. My Entries are at/near the 20 moving average. But you entered at candle open after the bearish engulfing candle. You will have bigger draw downs on your trade if you don't enter at/near the 20 moving average...and it will reduce your profits.   
  
As for exits...I use 75 pip target profits for pairs like GU, EJ, GJ and only 50 pip targets for EU, AU, UJ. Those are based on entries at/near the 20ma though! The farther you are away from the 20ma, then you have to adjust your profit target to something smaller! 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

> [Quoting freedomsg](/thread/post/4108863#post4108863 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi 211, EU after a short down trend, a Hammer form and follow by a bullish candle. Do we wait for it to retrace back to the low of the hammer area (which we can reduce our Sl) or wait for it to hit the 20ma and it is also somewhere near the fibo 50% level? The SOC cross and turning up at the moment. Thanks ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f44d.png?v=15.1)
> 
> Ignored

Hi Freedom,  
  
Very good question! Typically if you just enter at the retrace to the 20ma. And if the hammer area is fairly close to where the 20ma is, then you should be ok. However, if there is some big different like 50pips or more between the two...then you really need to take a look at price action at the 20ma and see if it's stalling or going through it...if it goes through it fairly easy, then you would most likely wait until it retrace to the hammer area. That's a very tough question ask no two trades are exactly alike!

Quite an interesting week...we had some pretty big swings in price. I would have posted this earlier, but I was busy with my day job. Anyway...we started out the week well with 2 winners for 125pips...and then finished the week with 1 loser of 100pips and and 1 winner for 50. So we would have finished up 75pips in profit...not too bad!  
  
The first chart shows the 2 EU trades...the first one was a loser and this does happen from time to time. No one has 100% winners. But the second trade made back some of the loss.  
  
The second chart shows GU and I decided not to trade that pair because price wasn't at the levels I would have liked to see. Reasons on posted on the chart.   
  
Have a good weekend everyone!

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar119267_2.gif) Krysztau](krysztau)

  * | Joined Oct 2009  | Status: Trader Zen | [134 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=119267)

> [Quoting tradelover09](/thread/post/4117827#post4117827 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi Chris,   
>    
>  What is it about this 4H trading approach that appeals to you? I look forward to more posts from you. I've been reading a lot of the threads on this site, and have found that everyone's perspective has been really helpful in learning the subtle in's and out's of forex trading. Good luck!
> 
> Ignored

HI,  
Actually I've sticked with J16 thread for some time, but it's too messy for me. No offence to anyone but there is that many participants, that I got confused.  
  
Personally I am not strict follower of "formations". I'd rather have a look and think, will it go further will it retrace now or later? If it retraces now, how far will it go, etc...  
  
Seeing the formation gives me a sort of benchmark - first I spot one, then I think - will I agree with that.  
  
I also really like 1M formations [I think I should open a new thread about it ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1)], and very often use 1M TF to enter trade signalled at 4H TF, and I always make fist SL adjstment from 1M point of view.  
  
I consider myself very near to profitability, since I have really nice strokes of winners, but than psychology goes into play and sudenly I feel not that convinient, or forced to do something, and than I do stupid things.  
  
If you'd like to see what I mean this is my demo equity curve:  
[http://www.myfxbook.com/portfolio/in...e-trader/35885](http://www.myfxbook.com/portfolio/intuitive-trader/35885)

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * Nov 2, 2010 8:35am  Nov 2, 2010 8:35am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar119267_2.gif) Krysztau](krysztau)

  * | Joined Oct 2009  | Status: Trader Zen | [134 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=119267)

Here is what I call a trade:  
Take a look at 4H EU. It has just bounced off 4H trendline up 2 candles ago, yet IF it will go back to 1.3864 to test recent dip it will already be below the trendline. In that case I bet it's going to get even lower. To 1.38 at least...  
  
And take MACD for a confirmation if you like it..

  * [#420](/thread/post/6110157#post6110157 "Post Permalink")

  * Oct 18, 2012 4:28pm  Oct 18, 2012 4:28pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar31376_12.gif) Tw0eleven](tw0eleven)

  * | Joined Jan 2007  | Status: Feed The Piggy With Pips! | [1,772 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=31376)

Hey everyone!!! WOW, it's been a long long time since I have visited this thread! To be honest, I'm quite surprised anyone is using it....I thought it died out a long time ago so I stopped keeping up with it. For those of you still using this method, how is it working for you???  
  
Just a little update about me...I have adjusted things and no longer use the 4hr method. In fact, I use a combination of the 15min chart and 1hr chart for trades and look for approximately 50pips per trade. Some of the basics in this new method are still the same(I use Price action, chart patterns and a few moving averages) and I use a Stochastics indicator instead of a macd now.  
  
When I get a little bit of free time, I'll try to post some charts on here and explain things. Probably this weekend at some point. Cheers!  
  
P.S. If you are using the 4hr method and it's profitable for you...GREAT! Glad it has helped. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

  * [#430](/thread/post/6128458#post6128458 "Post Permalink")

  * Oct 24, 2012 9:46pm  Oct 24, 2012 9:46pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar31376_12.gif) Tw0eleven](tw0eleven)

  * | Joined Jan 2007  | Status: Feed The Piggy With Pips! | [1,772 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=31376)

> [Quoting pama.fx](/thread/post/6119683#post6119683 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Glad to see your posting.  
>  Any chance you would share with us why no longer trade H4 tf?  
>    
>  A new thread for your lower tf would be a better option.  
>  What are the MAs?  
>    
>  Cheers
> 
> Ignored

While I think overall, the 4hr tf is less stressful...I just personally prefer to spend less time in the market(less risk). If I can take anywhere from 20-50pips per trade and only be in the trade for a couple hours or less I'm pretty happy. As we all know, the market doesn't move just one way...it's Up and Down...Moves/retraces. I'd just like to take a small amount of those moves...so that's why I switched.  
  
As for the ma's, they are your normal 50ema, 200ema and there is 13ema and 800ema. As we all know, the 50 and 200 are the ones most used by traders. And since I prefer using the 15minutes chart...the 13ema is there because it basically represent the 50MA on the 1hr chart( 13 times 4 = 52...pretty close to the 1hr 50). And the 800 would represent the 50ema on the 4hr chart( 800/4 = 200 on the 1hr and 200/4 = 50 on the 15min). So basically, with those 4 ema's on the 15min chart you get the 15min 50&200, the 1hr 50ema and the 4hr ema. The higher the MA, the stronger the support/resistance normally is.   
  
hope that helps.

> [Quoting dug_forex](/thread/post/6129373#post6129373 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi  
>    
>  I really like the system on M15, thankyou for sharing ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f44d.png?v=15.1). I am very interested in finding out more. I am interested in finding out more about how the moving averages are used to guage trend. I love the fact that it is very price action focused. Are candlesticks reliable on M15?
> 
> Ignored

  
They are reliable as long as you are backing it up with price patterns, the moving averages, stochastics...and it doesn't hurt to take a quick look at the 1hr and 4hr charts to make sure you aren't trading against any obivious price/candlestick pattern that contradicts the 15min chart.  
  
Again, use MUST use the candlestick patterns WITH other confirmations...not just by themselves. You want 3 or more reasons to enter a trade. Also, if you have 3 or more reasons NOT to enter a trade, it would probably be safer to stay out of a trade. Everyone needs to be disciplined and try to pick the BEST setups...NOT trade every setup! ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)
